Density functional theory for crystal-liquid interfaces of Lennard-Jones fluid 
Xin Wang; Jianguo Mi; Chongli Zhong
Crossmark: Check for Updates
Author & Article Information
J. Chem. Phys. 138, 164704 (2013)
https://doi.org/10.1063/1.4802633
Article history
Share 
Tools 
A density functional approach is presented to describe the crystal-liquid interfaces and crystal nucleations of Lennard-Jones fluid. Within the theoretical framework, the modified fundamental measure theory is applied to describe the free energy functional of hard sphere repulsion, and the weighted density method based on first order mean spherical approximation is used to describe the free energy contribution arising from the attractive interaction. The liquid-solid equilibria, density profiles within crystal cells and at liquid-solid interfaces, interfacial tensions, nucleation free energy barriers, and critical cluster sizes are calculated for face-centered-cubic and body-centered-cubic nucleus. Some results are in good agreement with available simulation data, indicating that the present model is quantitatively reliable in describing nucleation thermodynamics of Lennard-Jones fluid1 / 1ChatGPTChatGPT{{cite journal |last=Wang |first=Xin |author2=Mi, Jianguo |author3=Zhong, Chongli |title=Density functional theory for crystal-liquid interfaces of Lennard-Jones fluid |journal=The Journal of Chemical Physics |volume=138 |issue=16 |pages=164704 |year=2013 |doi=10.1063/1.4802633}}1 / 1A reference for this 1 / 1ChatGPTChatGPTI apologize, but I'm unable to provide a reference for a statement without any specific information or context. This article needs attention from an expert in WikiProject. The specific problem is: may need attention from a physicist or engineer. (January 2023)
A Lennard-Jones fluid is a computational model widely used in computational chemistry to study intermolecular interactions.[1] It is named after John Lennard-Jones, who introduced the Lennard-Jones potential, also known as the LJ potential or 12-6 potential, that describes the interactions between particles in the fluid. The LJ potential captures the essential features of electronically neutral atoms or molecules, including repulsive and attractive van der Waals interactions.[2]

The LJ potential is given by the equation:

{\displaystyle V_{\text{LJ}}(r)=4\varepsilon \left[\left({\frac {\sigma }{r}}\right)^{12}-\left({\frac {\sigma }{r}}\right)^{6}\right]}
{\displaystyle V_{\text{LJ}}(r)=4\varepsilon \left[\left({\frac {\sigma }{r}}\right)^{12}-\left({\frac {\sigma }{r}}\right)^{6}\right]}

Here, V represents the distance between two interacting particles, Îµ is the depth of the potential well (dispersion energy), and Ï is the distance at which the potential energy is zero (size of the particle). The LJ potential exhibits a repulsive force at very close distances, an attractive force at moderate distances, and no interaction at infinite distance.

Molecular dynamics simulations have been used to study the Lennard-Jones fluid under various state conditions. These simulations provide information about the pressure and configurational energy of the fluid at different densities and temperatures.

A comprehensive equation of state for the Lennard-Jones fluid has been derived by combining simulation results with values calculated from the virial series and second virial coefficients[3]. This equation of state, known as the modified BenedictâWebbâRubin equation, incorporates 33 constants and accurately describes the behavior of the Lennard-Jones fluid over a wide range of temperatures and densities.

Additionally, two- and three-body integrals (J, K, and L) that occur in perturbation theory for molecular fluids have been calculated for the Lennard-Jones fluid under various state conditions[4].

Good luck with completing the Wikipedia page!1 / 1Approaches based on adapters and sparse i netuning have also been proposed [Pfeiffer et al., 2020, 
2022, 2021, Ansell et al., 2022]. Adapters are bottleneck layers (usually placed after the feedforward 
layers) that add extra capacity when adapting to a different task or language. Our proposed forgetting 
mechanism can also be applied to adapter-based methods as we can allow forgetting to happen in 
the adapter layers. The current choice of forgetting embeddings keeps the architecture intact and 
incurs no additional hyperparameter tuning, allowing us to understand the fundamental capability of 
forgetting pretraining. 
6Conclusion & Future work 
6.1Conclusions 
While forgetting is usually perceived as negative, recent work point out that it can also be benef i cial in 
certain cases, particularly for quickly learning new tasks, training in non-stationary environments [Igl 
et al., 2021, Nikishin et al., 2022, DâOro et al., 2023] and improving sample eff i ciency [Taha et al., 
2021, Zhou et al., 2022]. Joining this line of work, our paper demonstrates that forgetting techniques 
can improve pretrained language models by imbuing them with more linguistic plasticity. Specif i cally, 
our proposed active forgetting mechanism can create PLMs that are easier to rewire for new lingual 
spaces. Experiments with RoBERTa show that models pretrained via active forgetting can better 
learn from small amounts of data while also enjoying faster convergence during language adaptation, 
particularly for languages distant from English. 
Going beyond language adaptation, we argue that rewirable PLMs are a promising direction for future 
research, as they allow easier adaptation to various tasks, domains, languages and can evolve faster 
as the real world changes. Unlike symbolic methods, such as knowledge graphs, which can easily 
rewire a fact by modifying the corresponding knowledge triplet, current static PLMs are harder to 
rewire since changing one fact via updating model weights may disrupt multiple other facts without 
substantial post-hoc intervention. Improving the rewirability via forgetting pretraining thus can be 
seen as one way of imbuing PLMs with similar benef i ts as symbolic methods (making the resulted 
model more controllable i.e. can be modif i ed with tiny cost), complementing the line of post-hoc 
model editing research [Mitchell et al., 2021, 2022]. 
6.2Limitations 
Our work considers the simplest form of forgetting: directly discarding the learned embedding 
weights and resetting them to some random initialization. Future work could consider more advanced 
forgetting techniques such as gradually injecting noise into the embedding weights. We focus 
on masked language modeling with language-specif i c tokenizers. It would be interesting to also 
investigate active forgetting for auto-regressive language modeling (e.g. the GPT family models) and 
various tokenizers. 
On the theory front, potential connections can be made between forgetting and meta-learning [Schaul 
and Schmidhuber, 2010, Thrun and Pratt, 2012, Andrychowicz et al., 2016, Finn et al., 2017] since 
both attempt to learn solutions that can quickly adapt themselves to new inputs. Another possible 
theoretical explanation for why active forgetting works so well might be related to the l atness of 
the solution in the loss landscape [Alabdulmohsin et al., 2021]. Flatter minima tend to enjoy better 
generalization [Liu et al., 2023]. Thus, it might be worthwhile to study the l atness of the transformer 
body during the forgetting pretraining.1 / 1ChatGPTChatGPTThe proposed active forgetting mechanism can be applied to adapter-based methods, which utilize bottleneck layers called adapters to add extra capacity for different tasks or languages [Pfeiffer et al., 2020, 2022, 2021, Ansell et al., 2022]. By allowing forgetting to occur in the adapter layers, the architecture can maintain its integrity without the need for additional hyperparameter tuning. This approach enhances the fundamental capability of forgetting pretraining.In conclusion, while forgetting is typically viewed as negative, recent research highlights its potential benefits, such as aiding in quick learning of new tasks, training in non-stationary environments, and improving sample efficiency [Igl et al., 2021, Nikishin et al., 2022, D'Oro et al., 2023, Taha et al., 2021, Zhou et al., 2022]. This study demonstrates that forgetting techniques can enhance pretrained language models (PLMs) by increasing their linguistic plasticity. The proposed active forgetting mechanism enables the creation of PLMs that are more easily adaptable to new linguistic spaces.The experiments conducted using RoBERTa show that models pretrained with active forgetting exhibit improved learning from limited data and faster convergence during language adaptation, especially for languages that are distant from English. This research suggests that rewirable PLMs, facilitated by active forgetting, are a promising direction for future investigation. These models can facilitate easier adaptation to diverse tasks, domains, and languages, allowing them to evolve quickly alongside real-world changes. By enhancing rewirability, PLMs can achieve benefits similar to symbolic methods, such as knowledge graphs, enabling efficient modifications with minimal cost. This complements existing research on post-hoc model editing [Mitchell et al., 2021, 2022].Some limitations of this work include the simplicity of the forgetting approach, which directly discards learned embedding weights and resets them to random initialization. Future studies could explore more advanced forgetting techniques, such as gradually injecting noise into the embedding weights. Additionally, while the focus of this research is on masked language modeling with language-specific tokenizers, investigating active forgetting in auto-regressive language modeling (e.g., GPT family models) and different tokenizers would be valuable.On the theoretical front, potential connections can be made between forgetting and meta-learning [Schaul and Schmidhuber, 2010, Thrun and Pratt, 2012, Andrychowicz et al., 2016, Finn et al., 2017], as both aim to learn solutions that can adapt quickly to new inputs. Another theoretical explanation for the efficacy of active forgetting may relate to the flatness of the solution in the loss landscape [Alabdulmohsin et al., 2021]. Flatter minima often exhibit better generalization [Liu et al., 2023], suggesting the value of studying the flatness of the transformer body during forgetting pretraining.1 / 1Jonathan Roberge & Tom Lebrun: Parrots All the Way Down51

as BERT and GPT-3 are becoming powerful interpreting machines, to say the 
least,which,ofcourse,isnotwithoutitsshareofclaims.Itwasthepurposeof

ciently. h e strength of Transformers lies in their flexibility: the relationship

However, I can try to provide some brief pointers or suggestions for each question.

Linguistic plasticity can be applied to other domains beyond language adaptation, such as machine learning and artificial intelligence, by considering how models can learn to adapt to changing environments, tasks, and data sources, and how they can leverage prior knowledge and experience to improve their performance and generalization. For example, meta-learning, transfer learning, and continual learning are some approaches that aim to achieve this kind of plasticity in machine learning and artificial intelligence.

The principles of forgetting and adaptation can be integrated into the development and training of language models, specifically those based on adapters and sparse fine-tuning, by using techniques such as elastic weight consolidation, dropout, pruning, distillation, or regularization to selectively forget or retain information from the pre-trained model, and by using adapters or sparse layers to fine-tune the model on specific tasks, languages, or domains. For example, the Reformer model uses reversible layers and local attention to reduce memory consumption and enable efficient fine-tuning.

Rewirable pre-trained language models have the potential to be more adaptable to different tasks, languages, and domains, by allowing the model to dynamically rewire its connections and parameters according to the input and output requirements. This could also enable more symbolic methods and post-hoc model editing research, by allowing the model to incorporate explicit rules or constraints into its representations and outputs. For example, the RNNbow model uses a rewiring mechanism to learn sparse and interpretable representations of natural language.

The notion of active forgetting in pre-training language models aligns with theories of meta-learning and the flatness of solutions in the loss landscape, by suggesting that forgetting can be a useful strategy to find more generalizable solutions that can perform well across different tasks and domains. The flatness of the transformer body during forgetting pretraining could provide insights into how the model learns to balance between specificity and generality, and how it allocates its capacity and complexity. For example, the FORGET-ME-NOT model uses active forgetting to improve the generalization of pre-trained language models.

The platformization and datafication of everyday life contribute to the dominance of tech giants like Google and the potential challenges of interpretability and explicability in AI systems, by creating a feedback loop between data collection, algorithmic optimization, and user behavior, which reinforces the power and influence of these platforms over various aspects of society. The interpretability and explicability of AI systems become more challenging as these systems become more complex, opaque, and ubiquitous, and as they affect more critical decisions and outcomes. For example, the Google search engine is an example of a platform that shapes how people access information and knowledge online.

The political and economic implications of AI and natural language processing are manifold, particularly in terms of power dynamics, distribution of resources, and the control exerted by major companies. AI and natural language processing can have positive impacts such as enhancing productivity, innovation, communication, education, etc., but they can also have negative impacts such as displacing workers, creating inequalities, manipulating opinions, infringing privacy, etc. The control exerted by major companies over AI and natural language processing can affect how these technologies are developed, deployed, regulated, and used. The issues of copyright and ownership of content generated by language models are also relevant, as they raise questions about the originality, authenticity, authorship, and value of such content. For example, the GPT-3 model is an example of a powerful language model that is controlled by a single company (OpenAI).

The Gebru affair sheds light on the relationship between AI, ethics, and power, by exposing the tensions and conflicts between the corporate interests and values of Google and the ethical and social concerns of some of its researchers, especially those from marginalized and underrepresented groups. The Gebru affair also reveals the challenges and risks of conducting and publishing critical research on AI within the industry, and the need for more independent, diverse, and inclusive voices in AI research. Critical hermeneutics and Critical AI Studies can contribute to a deeper understanding of the co-optation, marginalization, and silencing of criticism within the AI industry, by providing theoretical frameworks, methodologies, and perspectives to critically examine and challenge the assumptions, values, and impacts of AI systems. For example, the paper âOn the Dangers of Stochastic Parrots: Can Language Models Be Too Big?â is an example of critical research on AI that was rejected by Google.

Ricoeur sees the world as being constituted through language, where language both reflects and shapes our understanding of reality. Language is not just a tool for describing the world; it actively participates in the creation and interpretation of meaning.In the context of AI and natural language processing, the intersection of reality, interpretation, and signification becomes significant. Language models like BERT and GPT-3 aim to interpret and generate text, but their understanding is limited to statistical patterns and correlations in vast amounts of data. They lack a deeper grasp of the meaning and context behind the words they process.This raises questions about the implications of AI and natural language processing. Without a comprehensive understanding of the world, these models may produce outputs that are detached from human experience and values. The interpretation and signification of language become mechanistic and divorced from the rich tapestry of cultural, historical, and social contexts that give meaning to human communication.Ricoeur's philosophy emphasizes the importance of interpretation and understanding in engaging with texts and the world. The meaning of language emerges through a dialectical process of interpretation, where the reader brings their own understanding and engages in a dialogue with the text. This hermeneutic approach recognizes the situatedness of interpretation within a broader cultural and historical context.In the realm of AI and natural language processing, a critical hermeneutic perspective becomes essential. It calls for a nuanced understanding of the limitations and biases embedded in these systems, as well as the social and cultural implications of their use. It prompts us to question the power dynamics at play, who benefits or is marginalized, and how these systems shape the world of meaning.By considering the intersection of reality, interpretation, and signification, we can critically examine the role of AI and natural language processing in constructing and shaping the world of language. It calls for a responsible and reflexive approach that acknowledges the limitations of automation and emphasizes the need for human engagement, ethical considerations, and a broader understanding of meaning beyond statistical patterns.1 / 1Interconnections with the previous topics1 / 1ChatGPTChatGPTThe discussion of Ricoeur's concept of world and its relation to language and its automation intersects with several of the previous topics we've explored:Linguistic Plasticity: Ricoeur's understanding of language as constituting the world aligns with the idea of linguistic plasticity, which refers to the adaptive and flexible nature of language. Forgetting mechanisms and adaptive techniques can be explored to mitigate biases and improve fairness in language models.The role of pretraining in language models and its limitations: Pretraining is a crucial step in the development of language models, where they learn from vast amounts of data. However, pretraining alone may not be sufficient to address specific tasks or adapt to new contexts. The concepts of forgetting and adaptation become relevant here, as they allow language models to fine-tune on specific tasks, languages, or domains after pretraining.The potential benefits of forgetting mechanisms in pretrained language models: Forgetting mechanisms in pretrained language models can enable them to selectively retain or forget information, leading to more efficient memory usage and improved generalization. This is particularly valuable in scenarios where models need to adapt to new tasks or contexts while avoiding catastrophic forgetting.The relationship between forgetting and adaptation in language models: Forgetting and adaptation are closely connected in the context of language models. Forgetting allows models to adapt to new inputs or tasks by selectively discarding irrelevant or outdated information. This adaptability enhances the model's ability to learn new tasks or generalize to different contexts.The concept of linguistic plasticity and its implications for language adaptation: Linguistic plasticity refers to the ability of language to adapt and evolve in response to changing environments and communicative needs. Language models can benefit from this concept by incorporating mechanisms that enable them to adapt their representations and behaviors to different tasks, languages, or domains.The positive aspects of forgetting in certain contexts: Forgetting can be beneficial in certain contexts, such as quickly learning new tasks and improving sample efficiency. By forgetting irrelevant information, language models can focus on the most relevant features and improve their learning and performance.The connection between forgetting and meta-learning: Meta-learning is a learning paradigm that aims to enable models to learn how to learn, adapt, and generalize from past experiences. Forgetting mechanisms can be viewed as a form of meta-learning, where models learn to selectively retain important information while discarding less relevant information.The notion of meaning unfolding in textuality and the role of hermeneutics: Hermeneutics, as discussed earlier, helps us understand how meaning is constructed and interpreted in textuality. The concept of meaning unfolding relates to how language models interpret and generate text.
